# Jaclang Release Notes

This document provides a summary of new features, improvements, and bug fixes in each version of **Jaclang**. For details on changes that might require updates to your existing code, please refer to the [Breaking Changes](../breaking-changes.md) page.

## jaclang 0.30.2 (Latest Release)

### New Features

- **Feature: the Jac-native desktop host runs on the fused single-binary runtime**: instead of binding the build machine's `libpython` by soname (`INSTSONAME` + an `LD_LIBRARY_PATH`/RUNPATH to its `LIBDIR`), a desktop app now brings up the **same fused runtime the `jac` CLI ships** -- the pinned, bundled CPython + jaclang carried in the binary's trailer payload. The CPython bring-up (materialize the payload → set a hermetic env → `dlopen` the bundled libpython → pin the program name → resolve the C-API) is unified in `launcher/embed.zig`, shared by the headless CLI launcher and the desktop host. The desktop host reaches it through a small C-ABI shim, `libjacpyembed` (`launcher/pyembed.zig`): the generated `host.na.jac` imports it by logical name (`import from jacpyembed`, resolved as a `$ORIGIN` sibling -- no `patchelf` for libpython), and `jac_engine_boot()` materializes the trailer and initializes the interpreter. The build appends this `jac`'s `[payload][trailer]` onto the compiled host, so it carries the bundled runtime and **auto-dedupes to the CLI's `rt/<hash>` cache** (identical payload hash). The shim ships inside the payload (`--pyembed`) and is staged `$ORIGIN`-adjacent at build time. Net effect: no build-machine libpython, no `INSTSONAME`, no `LD_LIBRARY_PATH`, and no per-build "bake the builder's site-packages into the binary" step -- the desktop app is the jac engine plus a window.
- **Feature: desktop bootstrap modules are imported from the fused runtime**: `oauth_broker`, `inprocess_dispatch`, and the desktop plugins are no longer `jac2py`-transpiled and staged as `.py` beside the binary -- the embedded interpreter imports them straight from the bundled jaclang tree (the plugins via their runtime dir on `sys.path`, with `import registry` cascading to every `built_in.*` plugin). Removes three staging passes and their `jac2py`/`jac0` subprocesses; only the app's own `sv` source tree and `dist/` bundle are still staged.
- **Feature: `na`/LLVM is first-class in the desktop runtime**: because the desktop app bundles the same payload the CLI ships -- which carries the LLVMPY shim and the native compiler -- an app's runtime can drive `jac nacompile` / `na` exactly like the CLI.
- **Feature: In-process `sv` dispatch in the Jac-native desktop host** (Phase J4), now running on the fused runtime: `cl` → `sv` walker/function calls on the desktop target run through the embedded CPython in-process instead of an HTTP POST to a remote backend. `inprocess_dispatch` boots the jac-scale ASGI app over a Starlette `TestClient` (no socket) and serves as the native `window.__jac_invoke` trampoline with the same `{kind, name, node, fields, token}` request contract and `{status, ok, body}` reply semantics as the web API. Dispatch runs on a single serialized worker thread off the GTK UI thread so a slow walker never freezes the window, with a configurable per-call timeout (`NATIVE_DISPATCH_TIMEOUT`, non-preemptive) and a bounded queue (`NATIVE_DISPATCH_BUSY` on saturation) set via `[plugins.desktop.dispatch]` (`timeout_s`, `max_queue`) in `jac.toml`. If the in-process backend fails to boot, the host shows a deterministic native error page instead of navigating to a silently-broken app, and `dispatch()` returns a `NATIVE_BOOT_ERROR` envelope rather than hanging. Native error envelopes follow a production error contract (`{code, message, request_id}`): every error carries a `request_id` for log correlation, and full tracebacks go to stderr only -- echoed into `error.details` solely when debug is enabled via `[plugins.desktop.dispatch].debug` (or the `JAC_DESKTOP_DEBUG` env var). Until jac-scale is bundled into the fused runtime, `sv` dispatch resolves jac-scale from a portable runtime seam (`JAC_DESKTOP_SCALE_SRC` / `JAC_DESKTOP_DEPS`), with no build-machine state baked in.
- **Feature: Native desktop IPC bridge for walker/function calls**: `__doWalkerFetch` and `__doFuncFetch` in the `cl` runtime route through `globalThis.__jac_invoke` when `__JAC_NATIVE__` is set (the Jac-native desktop shell), carrying the frozen `{kind, name, node, fields, token}` request and replaying HTTP status/body semantics locally, including 401 → re-login for walkers.
- **Feature: native `str(float)` now emits CPython's shortest round-trip repr (#6978 Phase 0.3)**: `str`/`repr`/`print`/f-string/`str.format` of a float on the native (na) backend previously used a lossy `%g` (`str(1.0)` gave "1" on na vs "1.0" on sv). A memoized `__jac_float_repr` helper now finds the smallest precision whose `%.*e` rendering re-parses (`strtod`) to the exact double, then reformats in CPython's `'r'` style (exponential when `decpt <= -4` or `decpt > 16`, else fixed `%.*f` with a trailing `.0` for integral values; nan/inf/-inf spelled as CPython does). This closes the `json.dumps` bare-float parity gap, and a new equivalence test pins na/sv byte-equality across 33 doubles including subnormals, the max double, `-0.0`, and inf/nan.
- **Native: upgrade to LLVM 22 and range-fetch LLVM via slices**: The native (`na`) backend now builds on LLVM 22.1.8 (the `LLVMPY_*` shim re-vendored verbatim from llvmlite 0.48.0rc1). The Linux shim links against GNU libstdc++ to match the official LLVM 22 Linux release (statically, so the shipped shim stays self-contained); macOS continues via Apple `clang++`/libc++. `zig build fetch-llvm` now range-fetches only the ~84 MB the shim links (`lib/libLLVM*.a` + `llvm`/`llvm-c` headers, plus macOS `libLTO.dylib`) from the `jaseci-labs/llvm-slice` repackaged zip instead of the ~1 GB upstream `.tar.xz`, with linked archives verified against a pinned manifest checksum.
- **Feature: native programs can static-link a bundled C floor into the binary (#6978 Phase 0.1a)**: a clib floor import such as `import from lzma { def lzma_crc32(...) }` now links the library's static archive directly into the `nacompile` binary instead of carrying a runtime dylib dependency. New `ar` archive reader in `linker_common` (`parse_ar_archive`, `parse_ar_symbol_index`, `select_ar_members`) pulls only the transitively-needed members; `MachOLinker` gained multi-object merge (`archive_members`) with cross-object symbol resolution; and `nacompile` resolves the import to its bundled `lib<name>.a`, dropping it from the dylib dependency list. Verified on macOS arm64 (the TLS-free floor set): `import from lzma`/`import from expat` programs run with `otool -L` showing only libSystem. Mach-O only for now; ELF/PE keep the dylib path, and production payload staging of the archives is Phase 0.2.
- **Feature: `jac test` accepts multiple file paths**: `jac test a.jac b.jac` previously errored with "unrecognized arguments"; the path argument is now a multi-value positional (matching `jac check`/`jac lint`), while bare `jac test` and single-file runs are unchanged.
- **Feature: native programs can static-link a bundled C floor into ELF binaries (#6978 Phase 0.1a)**: extends the static C-archive linking from #6986 (Mach-O) to ELF and wires it into `jac nacompile`, so a clib floor import like `import from lzma { def lzma_crc32(...) }` links the bundled archive into a Linux binary instead of carrying a runtime `.so` dependency. Adds `nacompile --target linux` to cross-build ELF from any host. Two ELF-linker fixes were needed: a section-relative relocation from a merged archive member now resolves to the member's offset within the coalesced section (not the section base), and the injected `main` runs the merged `.init_array` constructors before entry (the bundled `_start` bypasses libc startup, so a floor member's load-time constructor would otherwise never run). Verified in Linux containers on x86_64 (constructor and multi-member floors) and arm64 (constructor-free floors); an arm64 ADRP/ADD relocation edge for constructor-heavy members remains a follow-up. macOS Mach-O is unaffected.
- **Feature: native C-floor archives are bundled into the payload so installed binaries can static-link them (#6978 Phase 0.2)**: `nacompile`'s static C-floor archive linking (Phase 0.1a) previously resolved archives only from the dev `.pbs-build` tree, so a shipped binary had nothing to link and silently fell back to a dynamic dylib dependency. `mkpayload` now stages a curated floor set (`lib{ssl,crypto,sqlite3,mpdec,lzma,bz2,expat,z,zstd}.a`, the bundled-C set the native stdlib roadmap targets; best-effort per file so macOS's absent `libz` is skipped) into `python/floor/<osarch>/`, plus certifi's `cacert.pem` into `python/floor/cacert.pem` for the future ssl floor. The `nacompile` locator (`_floor_lib_dir`, split into a pure `_resolve_floor_dir`) now resolves either the dev `.pbs-build` tree or the installed `python/floor/<osarch>` payload layout, arch-keyed so a cross-`--target` build never links the wrong arch; `JAC_NATIVE_FLOOR_DIR` and `JAC_NATIVE_CA_BUNDLE` override the lookup.

### Bug Fixes

- **Fix: clib struct pointer subscript read/write now lowers correctly (#6707, #6708)**: `buf[i]` and `buf[i] = val` on a clib struct pointer parameter previously hit `E5090` ("subscript/index access not supported"). Native function annotations are unstamped by the type checker, so clib struct parameters like `buf: Color` lowered to `i64` in LLVM via the `_resolve_jac_type` fallback, and the subscript path's `ir.PointerType` check was never satisfied. `NaIRGenPass` now tracks `clib_local_struct_names: dict[str, str]` (populated from `p.type_tag.tag` at function entry and from typed local annotations like `c: Color = ...`), so the read path emits `inttoptr(buf_i64, %Color*) → GEP([i]) → ptrtoint → i64` and the write path emits `inttoptr + GEP` for the destination followed by the appropriate struct copy (`%Color*` boxed, `%Color` by-value, or `i64` pointer-as-int). Field access on the subscript result (`c.r`) works via the existing `_codegen_field_access` `IntType → inttoptr` path, now that `_struct_name_of` also consults `clib_local_struct_names` for unstamped `Name` nodes.
- **Fix: native `datetime` now matches CPython for pre-1970 timestamps (#6954 follow-up)**: The bundled `na_stdlib/datetime.na.jac` computed the day split (`total // 86400`) and `weekday()` (`(epoch_day + 3) % 7`) with raw `//` and `%`. On the native (na) backend integer `//` lowers to LLVM `sdiv` (truncates toward zero) and `%` to `srem` (sign follows the dividend), whereas CPython floors both, so for any negative (pre-1970) POSIX timestamp the na backend silently diverged from the sv backend across day/hour/minute/second and weekday (e.g. `fromtimestamp(-86401.0)` gave `1969-12-31` on na vs CPython's `1969-12-30`). The module now uses floor-correct `_fdiv`/`_fmod` helpers for the day split and weekday, keeping the two backends congruent across the whole timestamp domain; positive timestamps are unaffected. A negative timestamp is pinned in the `prim_datetime` equivalence fixture as a regression guard.
- **Fix: static-field global lowering no longer hides real codegen errors**: `_register_static_fields` created each `static has` module global inside a bare `try { ... } except Exception { continue }` meant only to skip a name already lowered on a re-visited module. That also swallowed genuine codegen failures (bad type, malformed name) from `ir.GlobalVariable()` as if they were benign duplicates. It now checks the llvm module's own global table for the name and creates the global unconditionally otherwise, so only an actual duplicate is skipped and any other error surfaces normally.
- **Fix: native backend demotes un-lowerable abilities instead of crashing the compile (#6967)**: The `.na.jac` native pipeline is best-effort: an ability it cannot lower is supposed to fall back to its Python implementation, never abort the whole module's native compile. Two paths violated that. (1) Binding a void-typed value to a variable (e.g. `k = none_returning_call()`, or a cross-module call whose native return type collapsed to `void`) asserted deep in `_entry_alloca` -> `PointerType.as_pointer()` on a void pointee; `_codegen_assignment` now emits `E5090` for a void-typed binding so the enclosing ability demotes cleanly. (2) A hard Python exception raised mid-codegen of a method body (e.g. a `void` operand type mismatch in a binary op) propagated out of `_codegen_method` and aborted the entire module, because `_demote_method_if_unlowerable` only fired on emitted diagnostics, not raw exceptions; per-method body codegen is now wrapped so a demotable method converts the crash into `E5090` and falls back to Python, while construction-critical (`init`/`postinit`) and vtable methods still propagate. Together a module with some un-lowerable abilities now natively compiles the rest: the bootstrap lexer lowers 19 methods + 3 functions where it previously crashed with an `AssertionError`. Also quiets the deferred autonative self-acceleration's per-method "native seam" warnings via a thread-local (`JAC_NATIVE_DEBUG` still surfaces them) and documents the `[run] autonative` switch in `jac.toml`.
- **Fix: native `<enum> | None` return types lower to i64 instead of `void` (#6971)**: A native function declared `-> Color | None` collapsed its return type to `void`, so any caller that bound the result (`c = pick(...)`) could not lower (it failed LLVM verification with `value doesn't match function result type 'void'`, and the binding raised the E5090 void-binding diagnostic). When the type checker has not stamped a `.type` on the annotation, `_resolve_jac_type` falls back to the AST-based `_resolve_primitive_name`, which walks the union's sub-nodes and returns the first that resolves to a type; for `int | None` the `int` operand resolved first, but for a member the primitive table does not know (an enum or user struct) the walk fell through to the bare `None` operand, which resolves to `VoidType`. `_resolve_primitive_name` now peels a `T | None` union explicitly: it skips the `None` operand(s) and resolves the value member, deferring to the existing struct / i64 fallback for a non-primitive member, so `Color | None` lands on the same i64 + enum-marshalling path as a plain `-> Color` (the marshaller maps the ordinal back to the enum member, with the out-of-range sentinel mapping to `None`). This mirrors the `_lower_type` union branch (the TypeBase path) so both resolvers agree; plain `-> None` returns are unaffected. As a result the bootstrap lexer no longer has any void-binding demotions: its `lookup_keyword(text) -> TokenKind | None` now lowers across the module boundary.
- **Fix: py2jac emits valid Jac for match class patterns**: Fixed a bug where py2jac would produce invalid Jac code for match statements with class keyword patterns (`key=value`), because `MatchKVPair` was missing the operator token in its `kid` list and the unparse pass always emitted a hardcoded colon separator.
- **Fix: native mixed-type ternary emits valid IR (#6987)**: A ternary whose two branches needed a numeric coercion (e.g. `1.5 if c else 2`, or two different int widths) miscompiled on the native backend. `_codegen_if_else_expr` positioned the builder at the merge block and only then coerced the branch values, so the `sitofp` / `zext` cast was emitted into the merge block *ahead of* the `phi`. LLVM requires every PHI to be among the first instructions of its block, so the verifier rejected the module ("PHI nodes not grouped at top of basic block") and native compilation failed, even though the Python backend handled the same code fine. Each coercion cast is now emitted in its predecessor block, just before that block's branch to the merge block, leaving the phi at the top of the merge block, which mirrors how the binary-op and short-circuit boolean paths already coerce operands before branching. Same-type branches emit no cast and were never affected.

### Refactors

- **Perf: Cache filter introspection by lambda `__code__`**: `_filter_type_name` and `_filter_has_predicates` are now memoized via `functools.lru_cache` keyed on `filt.__code__` (through a `_CodeKey` carrier where the closure walk is still needed). Jac emits filter lambdas inline at the path-construction call site, so identity-keyed caches never hit; code-keyed caches collapse every fresh function-instance from the same source to one entry. On the LittleX5 `load_feed` profile this cut filter introspection from ~2.65s / 43% of `osp_spawn` per walker run to a single-digit number of `dis.get_instructions` and `inspect.getclosurevars` invocations across the whole benchmark.
- **Refactor: remove `jac bundle --precompile`**: The shipped `_precompiled/*.jir` bundle is a cold-start optimization, not a correctness requirement; the runtime lookup is version-keyed (`cpython-3XX`) and opportunistic, so a wheel built without it is fully valid and recompiles on first import. For PyPI plugin wheels the benefit only applied to consumers on the exact build-time Python and bloated an otherwise portable wheel, so the `--precompile` flag (and `_precompile_project`) are dropped from `jac bundle`, along with their use in the release workflows and release scripts. The native binary's own precompile path (`mkpayload`) is unchanged. With the flag gone, `find_package_dir` in `precompile_bytecode.jac` collapses to its single live pass (the `__init__.py` lookup); the namespace-package and last-resort passes were dead code (the former targeted the removed `jac-client`).

## jaclang 0.30.1

### Breaking Changes

- **Breaking: connect operator returns the RHS as-is (#6817)**: The connect operators (`++>`, `<++`, `<++>`, and the typed `+>:Edge:+>` form) no longer always wrap their result in a list. A connect expression now mirrors what it connects to -- connecting to a single node returns that node, and connecting to a list of nodes returns a list. The `(a ++> b)[0]` idiom used to unwrap a single connected node is no longer needed (and now errors); drop the trailing `[0]`. List connects and chaining (`a ++> b ++> c`) are unaffected.
- **Breaking: `jac/pyproject.toml` removed -- jaclang is the single binary, not a PyPI/editable package.** The clean break is complete: jaclang ships only as the self-contained `jac` binary (Zig launcher + bundled CPython), built with `zig build` from `jac.toml` (no setuptools/pyproject). There is no more `pip install -e ./jac`. CI and the dev `scripts/fresh_env.sh` build the binary (via the new `.github/actions/setup-jac` action) and put `jac` on PATH; plugins install with `jac install -e <plugin>` (deps go into the project venv, jaclang is host-provided by the binary). The binary now bundles `watchdog` (for `jac start --dev`) and `tomlkit` (format-preserving TOML writes), and `jac bundle --precompile` precompiles through the bundled interpreter, so no system Python, pip, or PyPI jaclang is required for any `jac` workflow.
- **Breaking: the `jaseci` meta-package is retired; releases are anchored on jaclang**: `pip install jaseci` is no longer published. jaclang ships as the native `jac` binary and is now the release anchor -- a release that bumps jaclang cuts the `v<version>` GitHub Release (marked latest) that carries the binaries, while plugins (byllm/jac-scale/jac-mcp) publish to PyPI independently. Install Jac with the one-line installer and add plugins via `jac install <plugin>`.
- **Breaking: hermetic, self-contained installs**: `jac` now works regardless of the surrounding environment (with or without a host Python), and third-party packages live only where you put them. `jac install <pkg>` and `jac install -e <path>` install into the current project's `.jac/venv` by default (and require a `jac.toml`); pass `--global` to install into the binary's own jac-owned site instead, for a plugin or tool you want importable from any project. Installs always run through the binary's bundled pip (no external `uv`); `.jac` module resolution and plugin discovery no longer consult the host's system/user `site-packages`; and an activated outside venv on `PATH` can no longer shift the interpreter's `sys.prefix`. `jac bundle --precompile` now precompiles for the bundled interpreter only (consumers on another Python recompile on first import).

### New Features

- **Feature: Solid (signals) client backend**: `framework = "solid"` now selects `SolidBackend`, the first fine-grained reactivity target for client codegen (`.cl.jac` / `cl {}` → JavaScript). Unlike the React/Preact re-render model, Solid runs each component body once and wires a reactive graph, so the backend exercises the read seams added in the prior phases: reactive state declarations lower to `createSignal`, value reads become accessor calls (`count()`) via `lower_state_read`, and dynamic JSX children/attributes become thunks (`() => count()`) via `lower_view_expr` so the runtime can re-track each binding. Writes route through the setter (`setCount(...)`); augmented assigns use a functional updater (`count += 1` → `setCount(prev => prev + 1)`) to avoid stale reads and self-subscription. Effects lower to `createEffect` (entry) and `onCleanup` (exit); the shared `__jacJsx` factory targets Solid's hyperscript runtime (`solid-js/h`), and `try/awaiting/except` slots lower to `<Suspense>`/`<ErrorBoundary>`. React/Preact output is unchanged (every new lowering is a no-op on the hooks backends). v1 is a best-effort subset over the representative fixtures; documented gaps (per the reactivity contract) include deferred `Ref[T]` fields (lowered to a plain `let` binding, no `ref={...}` wiring yet), block-level shadowing of reactive fields, the functional-updater asymmetry for plain self-referential assigns, true `createResource`-backed suspension, and full `dom-expressions` parity.
- **Feature: Solid runtime router + form parity**: the Solid runtime shim (`solid_runtime.cl.jac`) now exposes the same router, form, and error/async surface as the React shim, so `@jac/runtime` stays framework-identical for app code while a Solid build still pulls in **no** React-ecosystem package. Routing is backed by `@solidjs/router` through thin adapters that bridge the API-shape gap (`Link` → `A`, `to` → `href`, `Route element=` → `component=`; `Routes`/`Outlet` are best-effort shims), covering `Router`/`Routes`/`Route`/`Link`/`Navigate`/`Outlet`/`useNavigate`/`useLocation`/`useParams` plus the composed `useRouter` and `AuthGuard`. Forms use `@tanstack/solid-form` (`createForm`) with Zod schemas passed directly as Standard Schema validators (no resolver), so `useJacForm`/`JacForm`/`JacSchema` work without any `@hookform/*` package; per-field error messages stay reactive because the schema-driven `JacForm` reads `field.state.meta.errors`. (The form layer was later migrated to TanStack Form on both React and Solid in #6539; see that note for the current state.) Error/async parity (`JacClientErrorBoundary`/`ErrorFallback`/`JacAwaiting`) is built on `solid-js`'s `ErrorBoundary`/`Suspense`. A Solid project's default client dependencies are now framework-aware (`solid-js`, `@solidjs/router`, `@tanstack/solid-form`, `zod`; no React packages). File-based routing entry codegen is backend-aware (`_create_pages_entry_content` delegates to `build_pages_entry_script` for React and Solid). The simple Solid mount entry now wraps `app` in `JacClientErrorBoundary`, matching React/Preact. Runtime npm publishing rejects unknown peer packages instead of emitting an unbounded `"*"` range. Documented gaps pending browser e2e: nested-route matching through the `Routes` passthrough and true `Outlet` semantics on `@solidjs/router`.
- **Feature: View IR seam (phase 2)**: JSX lowering now builds a framework-neutral `ViewElement` tree in `EsJsxProcessor` (tag/attribute/child classification happens once) and hands it to `FrameworkBackend.lower_view`. React/Preact/Solid share `ReactBackend.lower_view`, which rebuilds the same `__jacJsx(tag, props, [children])` call; dynamic positions are thunked inside `lower_view` via `lower_view_expr` (no-op on hooks backends). Attribute kinds (`StaticAttr`/`DynamicAttr`/`EventAttr`/`RefAttr`) are classified in the producer so event handlers and `ref` never pass through the view thunk seam. React/Preact output is unchanged (zero-diff gate preserved).
- **Feature: native Solid file-based routing (phase 2)**: the generated Solid pages entry now targets `@solidjs/router` natively: `<Route>` children sit directly under `<Router>` (no `<Routes>`), routes use `component={Page}`, protected routes nest under a pathless `AuthGuard` route that renders `props.children`, and root layouts ride `<Router root={__jacMakeLayoutRoot(Layout)}>`. `Outlet` bridges Jac layout authoring (`<Outlet/>` in a param-less layout) to Solid Router's `props.children` via `__JacOutletContext`. jsdom routing fixtures exercise flat, nested, auth-guard, and layout routes.
- **Desktop Plugin IPC: OS capabilities for webview apps**: Desktop apps now expose a plugin host with seven built-in plugins (`path`, `window`, `fs`, `notification`, `clipboard`, `dialog`, `shell`) to JS via `window.__jac.invoke()` and `window.__jac.on()`, with per-plugin security gates (allow-lists, opt-in toggles, and deny-all shell defaults) configured under `[plugins.desktop.plugins]` in `jac.toml`. A typed `@jac/desktop` client SDK, plugin manifest, and registry ship alongside; the native host bootstraps the built-in plugins at startup and transpiles plugin `.jac` sources at build time. The `todo_app` example shows the least-privilege capability config and typed `@jac/desktop` SDK usage, and plugin build failures now print the full Python traceback.
- **Client Compiler: `@jac/*` modules resolve via entry points**: Packages can register virtual `@jac/*` modules through the `jac.modules` entry-point group so `@jac/desktop` and similar SDKs resolve without vendoring into jaclang. The Vite bundler now compiles a resolvable `@jac/desktop` SDK to `compiled/desktop_api.js` and wires the alias when present.
- **Native Compiler: SubTag type annotations lower correctly**: Native `_resolve_jac_type` unwraps `SubTag` wrappers so annotated globals and clib fields (e.g. `Callable[...]`) resolve to the correct LLVM types without re-reading `type_tag.tag`.
- **Feature: Exported symbols for native executables**: `jac nacompile` can now export defined symbols into an executable's `.dynsym` so they resolve via `dlsym`/`RTLD_NEXT` (e.g. exporting `close()` for the CEF zygote), and appends `libc.so.6`/`libm.so.6` last in `DT_NEEDED` so libcef's `.init_array` `dlsym(RTLD_NEXT, "close")` resolves correctly. (jaseci-labs/jaseci#6572)
- **Feature: CEF desktop target (`cef`)**: New `CefDesktopTarget` provides a Chromium Embedded Framework renderer alongside the OS-native webview. Set `engine = "cef"` under `[plugins.desktop]` and build with `jac build --client cef`. The loopback server and OAuth broker are shared with the native target; CEF integration is Jac-native (`cef.na.jac` + `libcef_dispatch.so` + `cef-subprocess`) with a pinned CEF 119.x binary fetch and an ABI guard for the verified `libcef.so` version. (jaseci-labs/jaseci#6572)
- **Feature: CEF smoke-test example**: New `notes-app` example exercises the CEF desktop target end-to-end (`jac build --client cef`) and includes desktop bridge, loopback broker, and localStorage diagnostics. (jaseci-labs/jaseci#6572)
- **Feature: access-modifier enforcement (`:pub` / `:protect` / `:priv`)**: a new `AccessCheckPass` (in the type-check schedule) enforces the access tags along two axes, chosen by where a symbol is declared. For members (`has`/`def` inside an archetype): `:pub` is accessible anywhere, `:protect` in the declaring class and its subclasses, `:priv` in the declaring class only. For top-level symbols (`glob`/`obj`/`def`/`enum`/`walker`): `:pub` is visible from any module including a consuming project (an exported library endpoint, so it need not be referenced inside its own project), `:protect` is visible within the same project (the directory tree rooted at its `jac.toml`), and `:priv` is visible only in the declaring module. Violations are warnings by default and promoted to hard errors with `[check] enforce_access = true` in `jac.toml`. New diagnostics `E/W2034` (private member), `E/W2035` (protected member), `E/W2037` (module-private cross-module), and `E/W2038` (project-protected cross-project) are individually suppressible via the existing `[check] suppress` / `# jac:ignore[...]` mechanisms. Endpoint/`:pub` behavior (`jac serve`, eject auth) is unchanged -- these rules govern call/reference legality, not endpoint surfacing.
- **Fix: `glob :priv` / `glob :protect` access modifier was dropped**: a module-private or project-protected global had its access silently reset to public because the assignment target was bound before the access-carrying global-var insert; module-private globals now enforce correctly.
- **Feature: Single self-contained `jac` binary**: `jaclang` now ships as one native executable (a Zig launcher that `dlopen`s a bundled CPython and runs the core in-process) built with a single `zig build`. No system Python, uv, or pip is required at install or runtime, and `jac test` runs the suite through the binary. The binary is the distribution -- jaclang is no longer published to PyPI; plugins consume jaclang as a host dependency.
- **Feature: native `jac` binary released for all four platforms**: The release pipeline now builds and attaches the self-contained `jac` binary for `linux-x86_64`, `linux-aarch64`, `macos-x86_64`, and `macos-aarch64` (one native runner each), matching every platform the installer detects. The obsolete pex/scie standalone build (which pip-installed `jaseci` from PyPI and could no longer resolve `jaclang`) was removed; the native binary built by the release-publish workflow is the sole distribution. `scripts/install.sh` downloads this binary, and the installer CI now tests that download/run/uninstall path.
- **Build: bundled CPython 3.14 and leaner typeshed**: the single `jac` binary now embeds Python 3.14 (python-build-standalone `cpython-3.14.6`, `llvmlite>=0.47`) and ships only the typeshed **stdlib** stubs. Third-party type stubs are no longer bundled: install the matching `types-*` package into your project (`jac add types-foo`) and the checker resolves it via PEP 561 `<pkg>-stubs` from the `.jac/venv`, so types track the installed version instead of a vendored snapshot. The typeshed git submodule is removed; stdlib stubs are fetched at a pinned commit (`launcher/fetch-typeshed.sh`), gitignored rather than committed. Running from a source checkout now needs a one-time `launcher/fetch-typeshed.sh`, which `zig build` runs automatically.
- **Feature: editable jaclang dev loop (`[dev] jaclang_source`)**: the self-contained `jac` binary runs its own bundled copy of jaclang, so edits to the in-repo `jac/jaclang` source previously required a full `zig build` to take effect. Declaring `[dev] jaclang_source = "<dir containing jaclang/>"` in the nearest `jac.toml` now reroutes `import jaclang` to that source tree -- `sitecustomize` prepends it to the front of `sys.path` at startup (before the launcher boots jaclang), so compiler/pass/CLI/runtime edits run live with no rebuild. The override sets `JAC_NO_PRECOMPILE=1` to skip the shipped precompiled JIR bundle; the per-module cache is content-keyed, so edits self-invalidate. A cheap substring guard keeps non-dev startup free of the `tomllib` parse. Requires a one-time `zig build`, since `sitecustomize.py` ships inside the binary payload.
- **`[dev] test_jobs` configures the test runner's worker count**: `jac test` now reads the default xdist worker count from `[dev] test_jobs` in `jac.toml` (`"auto"` = one worker per core, `"0"` = serial, or a fixed count like `"4"`), so you no longer have to prefix every run with `JAC_TEST_JOBS=`. The `JAC_TEST_JOBS` environment variable still overrides the config when set.
- **Native `isinstance()` over user-defined types**: The native backend now lowers `isinstance(x, MyClass)` and `isinstance(x, (A, B))` via an inheritance-aware vtable-identity check (matching the target class and all its subclasses, correct under multiple inheritance), and narrows field access inside the guard so `x.field` resolves on the narrowed type. Previously these raised a "native pathway does not yet support" error (E5090).
- **Feature: native `__class__.__name__` / `type(self).__name__`**: both forms now lower in native (`na` / `.na.jac`) code instead of raising `E5090` (#6930 workstream A2). The result is runtime-correct: a class with a vtable reads its name from the instance's vtable, so an inherited base method reports the concrete subclass name, while a vtable-less class lowers to a constant string load. This also fixes a type-checker bug where any `@<prop>.setter` / `.getter` / `.deleter` decorator raised a bogus `E1031` ("Cannot access attribute 'setter'") under type checking, because a `@property` getter resolved to a function rather than a property object.
- **Native: partial-native classes / per-method opt-out**: A native-eligible class may now contain methods the native backend cannot lower (e.g. one using `eval`) without poisoning its whole module's native compile. Such a method is demoted to its Python implementation while the class keeps its native layout, native constructor, and lowerable sibling methods; construction-critical `init`/`postinit` gaps remain hard errors. Each demotion prints a terminal warning naming the method so a silent native fallback is visible during a build; set `warn_native_seams = false` under `[check]` in `jac.toml` for quiet builds (`JAC_NATIVE_DEBUG=1` forces the warning on regardless).
- **Native: foreign-typed fields lower to opaque null slots**: A native (`na`) `has` field whose declared type the backend cannot model (a foreign Python type such as `ast3.AST | None` or `type[Transform]`) now lowers to a nullable opaque slot (null at native construction) instead of rejecting the declaration with E5090; a type-only foreign import that merely names such a type is tolerated, while a genuinely unknown type name still reports E2018 and any actual dereference of the slot still reports E5090.
- **Feature: Decouple the native (`na`) backend from the Python `llvmlite` package**: the LLVM IR builder and the ctypes binding over the `LLVMPY_*` C ABI are now first-party Jac code under `jaclang/compiler/passes/native/llvm/` (py2jac-translated from llvmlite 0.47.0, BSD-2), and the verbatim C++ `LLVMPY_*` shim lives at `jac/native/`. A new `zig build jacllvm -Dllvm-dir=...` step compiles the shim and statically links a host LLVM 20.1.x into `libjacllvm.so` (the in-tree replacement for the bundled 167 MB `libllvmlite.so`). No `import llvmlite` remains in the runtime; a guard test enforces it. See #6925.
- **Feature: Bundled native standard library (`na_stdlib`) + `os.path`**: the native (`na`) pathway can now ship pure-Jac standard-library modules under `jaclang/runtimelib/na_stdlib/`, so `import from <mod> { fn }` resolves a bundled `.na.jac` module and links it through the existing cross-module machinery with zero per-module backend work: the same source binds CPython's real module on the sv pathway and the bundled one on na. Resolution is **nearest-wins**: the single shared `resolve_native_module` (used by `BoundaryAnalysisPass`, `NaIRGenPass`, and `NativeCompilePass`) searches the importing project's own tree first and falls back to the bundled root only on a miss, so a user module of the same name always shadows a bundled one. `NativeCompilePass`'s link-set discovery gained the matching bundled-root fallback so a bundled dependency's object code (`__jac_glob_init_<mod>`) is compiled and linked into both AOT (`jac nacompile`) standalone binaries and the JIT engine. The first bundled module is **`os.path`** (POSIX): `normpath`/`dirname`/`basename`/`split`/`splitext`/`isabs`, byte-for-byte congruent with CPython `posixpath` (including the collapsed-slash / `..`-resolution / leading-dot edge cases), pinned by the new `prim_ospath.jac` tri-backend equivalence test.
- **Feature: native `zlib` standard library over an FFI floor (#6940 Phase 2)**: `import from zlib { compress, decompress, crc32, adler32 }` now resolves to a bundled `na_stdlib/zlib.na.jac` on the native (`na`) pathway (and binds CPython's `zlib` on the sv pathway, the same source on both). It follows the FFI-floor + pure-Jac-surface architecture: the DEFLATE engine is the system `libz` reached through a thin FFI binding (`_zlib_native.na.jac`, Mechanism F, libz bound by logical name `z`), with the Python-shaped API (CPython argument orders and defaults, zlib-format streams, byte-for-byte congruent compressed output, grow-on-demand `decompress`) layered on top. To make foreign byte I/O work, a `bytes`/`bytearray` argument to a clib function now lowers to its raw data pointer (the C buffer-protocol convention) rather than the internal jacbytes `{ i64 len, [n x i8] }` struct pointer, so C no longer reads the 8-byte length header as leading data. A tri-backend equivalence fixture pins sv/na congruence on the checksums and the compress/decompress round-trip.
- **Build: `zig build -Ddev` editable dev binary (linked compiler)**: a build mode for compiler work that ships the `jac` binary **without** a bundled jaclang -- it bakes an absolute path to a compiler source dir into the payload and reroutes `import jaclang` there at startup, from any directory (no `[dev] jaclang_source` `jac.toml` stanza required in scope). Because nothing is bundled, the build skips both the ~100 MB compiler-tree copy and the JIR precompile, so it is much faster and ~65% smaller than a release binary; `scripts/fresh_env.sh` now uses it. `-Ddev` links the build root; `-Djaclang-dir=PATH` links an explicit dir. The binary hard-depends on that source tree (dev-only, not distributable) and -- since the compile schedule imports the native passes -- still needs the LLVMPY_* shim placed in-tree (`zig build fetch-llvm`, which `-Ddev` then compiles and places; the build stops with a clear message if it is missing). Builds on the editable dev loop (#6915).
- **Feature: Native stdlib `urllib.request` over a libcurl floor + variadic FFI (#6940 Phase 3)**: the native (`na`) pathway can now fetch over HTTP. A bundled `na_stdlib/urllib/request.na.jac` exposes `urlopen(url)`, which performs a real HTTP/1.1 GET -- DNS, TLS, and redirect following -- over **libcurl** reached through the native FFI (**Mechanism F**), not a reimplemented transport stack: libcurl abstracts the per-OS TLS backend (SecureTransport / OpenSSL / Schannel), so one binding covers every native host. The easy handle streams the response body and headers to temp `FILE*`s via libcurl's default `fwrite` callback (`CURLOPT_WRITEDATA` / `CURLOPT_HEADERDATA`), which the module reads back with the native `open().read()` builtin and parses into an `HTTPResponse` record (status, body length, reason, url, body, headers). Enabling this, the native FFI gained **variadic C declarations**: a trailing `*rest` param on a clib `def` (e.g. `curl_easy_setopt(handle, option, *rest)`) marks the symbol variadic so the backend emits a `var_arg` declaration over the fixed params -- required because on AArch64/AAPCS a variadic argument must pass on the stack, where a fixed declaration would wrongly pass it in a register and the value never reaches the callee. Pinned sv<->na congruent by the new `test_urllib_equivalence.jac`, which stands up a loopback `http.server` (no live network) and compares the bundled native `urlopen` against CPython's real `urllib.request` on HTTP status and received body length, for a direct GET and a 301 redirect both follow. Native-host-only (clean E5090 on wasm); partial coverage per #6940 (v1 is GET + redirects; `Request`/`Range`, POST, `timeout`, response accessor methods, and `HTTPError` on 4xx/5xx are documented next slices). Extends #6404; follows #6941.
- **Native stdlib (#6940 Phase 1): bundled `json` + `os.makedirs`/`os.path.realpath`**: A new bundled `na_stdlib/json.na.jac` ships a pure-Jac (Mechanism B) `json.loads` (recursive-descent parser over boxed `any`: dict/list/str/int/float/bool/None, with full string escapes and int-vs-float parsing) and `json.dumps` (CPython-default `(', ', ': ')` separators, insertion-ordered keys), so the same `import from json { loads, dumps }` binds CPython `json` on the sv pathway and the native module on na. The `os` intercepts gain `makedirs` (a `mkdir -p` loop over libc `mkdir`) and `os.path.realpath` (libc `realpath(3)`, non-strict). A supporting native-backend fix gives a boxed `None` its own JacVal tag instead of masquerading as a null string (which made `isinstance(None, str)` true and crashed `str`/`len`/iteration on it), so `json.dumps(None)` and null object values work. Known divergences: `dumps` of a bare float uses `str(float)` (`%g`) rather than the shortest-round-trip repr (gated on the Ryu float repr, Phase 0.3), and string escaping is ASCII-congruent (`ensure_ascii` of non-ASCII is a follow-up).
- **Native (#6951): static methods + class attributes, and a bundled `datetime`**: The native (na) pathway now lowers static-method calls (`ClassName.method(args)` on a `static def`) and class-attribute reads (`ClassName.attr` on a `static has`) on user classes, resolved through the MRO so subclasses inherit statics, and working both same-module and cross-module (a `Class.method(...)` call on an imported class now pulls the class's defining module into the native link set). Riding this, a new bundled `na_stdlib/datetime.na.jac` ships a UTC `datetime`/`timezone` pair where the same `import from datetime { datetime, timezone }` binds CPython `datetime` on the sv pathway and the native module on na: `timezone.utc` is a class attribute and `datetime.now`/`datetime.fromtimestamp` are class-level constructors, with the civil date computed from the POSIX epoch (Hinnant's days->civil) so `year`/`month`/`day`/`hour`/`minute`/`second`, `weekday()`, and `isoformat()` match CPython exactly for a fixed timestamp. Scope is UTC / fixed-offset only (no tz database, DST, leap seconds, or microseconds).

### Bug Fixes

- **Fix: `bytes + str` now reports a type error**: Adding `bytes` and `str` together was silently accepted by the type checker; it is now flagged, matching Python's runtime `TypeError`.
- **Fix: jac0 parses `static has` declarations (class-level constants)**: jac0's parser routed every `static` token to `_parse_funcdef` (which expected `static def`/`static can`), so `static has` hit a `ParseError` on the type-annotation colon and fell back to `jac2py`. The `jac2py` output retains `from jaclang...` imports that the embedded stdlib-only CPython in desktop hosts cannot load, which broke the loopback server in both `cef` and native `desktop` targets (`desktop_plugin.jac` was the affected file). The fix dispatches `static has` to `_parse_has` in both `_parse_item` and `_parse_enum_body`. (jaseci-labs/jaseci#6572)
- **Fix: Windows native executable build now emits COFF instead of ELF (#6819)**: `jac nacompile`'s executable branch created its target machine with the default `codemodel="jitdefault"`. llvmlite appends `-elf` to the target triple when `os.name == "nt"` and the code model is `"jitdefault"`, so on a Windows host the executable build emitted an ELF object for a COFF target and the object-format guard tripped (the shared/DLL branch already passed `codemodel="small"` and was unaffected, but the exe is built first). The executable branch and `NaIRGenPass.postinit` now pass an explicit `codemodel="large"`. `"jitdefault"` resolves to the large model on x86_64, so this preserves the relocations the pure-Jac ELF linker already handles; the small/medium models emit `R_X86_64_32` absolutes it cannot resolve. No change on Linux: the native binary build is byte-for-byte identical.
- **Fix: macOS/Windows shared-library exports resolve through `ctypes`/`dlopen`**: (macOS) the native linker no longer emits an `LC_LOAD_DYLINKER` load command in Mach-O dylibs (it is only valid for executables and could cause `dlopen` to reject the file) and defaults `CS_EXECSEG_MAIN_BINARY`'s `execSegFlags` to 0 for dylibs (the `0x1` main-binary flag is only valid on an executable's `__TEXT` segment and trips a macOS load error when set on a shared library). (Windows) the per-symbol `clib_symbol_lib` map now propagates transitively from imported `.na.jac` sub-modules to the entry module's import-table generation: previously only `clib_paths` crossed the module boundary while `clib_symbol_lib` was dropped, so every Win32 API symbol imported from a sub-module fell back to `needed_libs[0]` (`msvcrt.dll`) and the loader raised `WinError 127` at runtime. Single-file programs were always correct (the symbol-to-DLL map is built directly on the entry module during IR gen, no propagation needed). Added Mach-O `dlopen`/`dlsym` round-trip and export-trie naming regression tests (macOS-gated), a single-file `clib_symbol_lib` attribution guard, and the existing structural load-command guards.
- **Fix: Multiple `with entry` blocks in a native module (#6660)**: `jac nacompile` on a `.na.jac` module with two or more module-level `with entry { ... }` blocks crashed during IR generation with `llvmlite.ir._utils.DuplicatedNameError: jac_entry`, because the native backend emitted a separate `jac_entry` function per block. The blocks are now concatenated, in source order, into a single `jac_entry` (with the glob-init / `JAC_NO_GC` / imported-module init preamble emitted exactly once), mirroring the Python target. Single-entry modules are unchanged. As a guard against the whole class of bug, every fixed-name native runtime singleton (`jac_entry`, `__jac_glob_init`, the `__rc_*` / `__jac_exc_*` / `__osp_*` helpers) is now defined through a single `_define_function` helper that raises a clear internal error naming the symbol if an emitter is reached twice, instead of an opaque llvmlite `DuplicatedNameError`.
- **Fix: `jac ai --ui` no longer fails looking for the removed `jac-client` package**: The web-UI launcher checked for an installed `jac_client` module and aborted with a now-impossible `pip install jac-client` hint. The client framework ships in `jaclang` core, so the check is gone and `jac ai --ui` works with no extra install. CLI help text, the bundled skills, and the docs were also updated so the full-stack client/desktop project kinds are described as built into core (no plugin install).
- **Fix: jaclang-internal type stubs leaking into the user program's module hub**: `_resolve_program` now resolves symlinks (`os.path.realpath`) on both the jaclang root and the candidate module path before deciding whether a file is a jaclang-internal stub (typeshed/builtins `.pyi`) or user code. Previously it used `os.path.normpath`, which does not resolve symlinks, so when jaclang is materialized under a symlinked directory (e.g. the single binary's cache, or macOS `/var` -> `/private/var`) the internal stubs were routed into the user program's `mod.hub` instead of the compiler's internal hub. This also lets the test suite run unchanged through the single `jac` binary.
- **Fix: `jac nacompile` no longer mis-types unannotated locals bound to imported struct factories (#6868)**: When an entry module imported a struct factory whose return annotation the type checker had left unstamped (`_resolve_jac_type` saw `.type is None`), the native codegen defaulted the lowered type to `i64`. Locals bound to such imported factories were therefore lowered as scalars, and subsequent field access tripped `E5090` on a non-struct value. The lowering now falls back to the `struct_types` name registry before defaulting to `i64`, mirroring the existing lookup in `_lower_class_type`, so unannotated imports resolve to the correct struct pointer.
- **Fix: `auth_redirect` in `jac.toml` now works in file-based routing**: Setting `[plugins.client.routing] auth_redirect = "/dashboard"` now correctly redirects unauthenticated users to the configured path instead of always falling back to `/login`.
- **Fix: type narrowing now reaches comprehensions inside `if x is not None` (#6731)**: A comprehension in the body of an `if x is not None { ... }` guard no longer raises a spurious `E1001` (e.g. `Cannot assign list[NoneType] to list[Box]`). Inside the guard, `x` is correctly treated as non-`None`, so `[x for _ in range(3)]` type-checks as expected, for list, set, dict, and generator comprehensions. Genuine errors are still reported: dereferencing `x` in a branch where it really is `None` continues to error.
- **Fix: `jac nacompile --shared` initializes module-global clib structs on load (#6917)**: `_inject_shared_init` collapsed its own-module glob-init detection to a single unquoted substring scan (`"@__jac_glob_init("`), but LLVM quotes the symbol -- the emitted IR is `define void @"__jac_glob_init"()` -- so the scan missed it and `__jac_shared_init` was generated empty. The global's initializer never ran on `dlopen`, the struct-pointer slot stayed NULL, and the first field write/read into a global clib struct segfaulted (the desktop-cef target died here in `cef_dispatch_settings_create` before `cef_initialize`). The same code built as a plain executable was always correct: the JIT path resolves the init via `get_function_address`, immune to the text scan. The detection now checks both the quoted and unquoted forms, matching the transitive-source branch. Added a unit test on the production emitter (the quoted-symbol guard) and an end-to-end `--shared` global-clib-struct fixture + dlopen test; the shared-lib test helper was rerouted through the real `_inject_shared_init` so the suite exercises the production injection path instead of a divergent copy (the divergence is what let this slip past the whole file).
- **Fix: ANSI color codes no longer leak into redirected/non-TTY streams**: The base ANSI `ConsoleRenderer` now checks `isatty()` on the *target* stream at emit time, not just the global `use_color` flag resolved from `sys.stdout` at startup. `jac build 2>errors.log` with an interactive terminal no longer writes raw escape codes into `errors.log`, and `console.print(..., file=sink)` stays plain text for any non-TTY sink.
- **Editable dev loop now active when running from `jac/`**: The `[dev] jaclang_source` dev loop is read from the nearest `jac.toml`, so `cd jac && jac test tests` previously fell back to the binary's bundled jaclang (and ignored your source edits) because `jac/jac.toml` carried no `[dev]` stanza. `jac/jac.toml` now declares it alongside the repo root, so the loop holds from the jaclang dir. Set `JAC_NO_DEV_SOURCE=1` to force the loop off for a single command (e.g. to test the shipped bundled + precompiled jaclang).
- **Fix: `py2jac` handles implicit string concat across a backslash line-continuation (#6928)**: Converting Python where adjacent string literals were joined by an explicit `\` line-continuation (`"abc" \` ⏎ `"def"`) leaked the source backslash into the emitted Jac, producing unparsable output, and `py2jac` exited `0` with empty stdout, silently dropping the file in batch ports. `PyastBuildPass` now strips line-continuation backslashes that sit outside a string literal while preserving those inside one (and triple-quoted multilines), and `jac py2jac` exits non-zero when the conversion produces errors.
- **Fix: Build the native (`na`) LLVMPY_* shim on macOS**: the wheel-free shim now links with Apple `clang++`/`ld64` instead of Zig's linker, which cannot link LLVM's official macOS-ARM64 release archives (the self-hosted Mach-O linker rejects edge-case object members, and Zig 0.16 has no LLD Mach-O backend). Linux keeps the Zig linker path. Restores `test-native-macos` and the `macos-14` release binary. See #6938.
- **Fix: native `any`/`str()` gaps for a pure-Jac stdlib (#6943)**: The native (`na`) backend now handles the produce/consume-`any` operations a pure-Jac `json` needs. `str(None)` returns `"None"` (was a SIGSEGV on a null deref) and `str(True)`/`str(False)` return `"True"`/`"False"` (was `"1"`/`"0"`); an `isinstance`-guarded `any`→`dict` consume that accumulated a string under a loop no longer use-after-frees the accumulator (loop-iteration cleanup no longer releases a variable declared outside the loop body); subscripting (`x["k"]`/`x[i]`), iterating (`for e in x`), and `len()` now work on a runtime-typed `any` holding the canonical `dict[str, any]`/`list[any]` layout; an empty `list[any] = []` literal compiles; `str.strip`/`lstrip`/`rstrip` honor a character-set argument; and an empty string is correctly falsy in a ternary condition.
- **Fix: `-Ddev` binary no longer bricked by `JAC_NO_DEV_SOURCE`**: a linked `zig build -Ddev` binary (#6948) ships no bundled jaclang, so the baked `jac_linked_source` marker is its only compiler. `apply_dev_source_override` now resolves that marker *before* the `JAC_NO_DEV_SOURCE` guard, so the flag (which means "use the shipped compiler, not a dev tree") no longer leaves a linked binary with no source on `sys.path` and a crash on the first `.jac` import; `JAC_NO_DEV_SOURCE` continues to suppress only the `jac.toml`-based dev loop. Also caps `mkpayload`'s argv collection at the array size so a 17+ argument invocation can't index past the fixed buffer.
- **Fix: native `zlib.decompress` of large/highly-compressible payloads (#6940 Phase 2 follow-up)**: a C `int` libz status widened to Jac's 64-bit `int` zero-extended, so `Z_BUF_ERROR` (-5) arrived as `4294967291` and `decompress`'s grow-on-demand retry never fired, so it raised on any stream whose decompressed size exceeded its input-relative initial buffer estimate. The FFI floor now folds libz status codes back to signed before comparison. Also tightens the foreign-call `bytes`→data-pointer lowering to require the declared parameter actually be an `i8*` (so a `bytes` value handed to a non-pointer slot surfaces a type mismatch instead of silently producing a pointer), and documents the libz `uLong` width (LP64 vs Windows LLP64) assumption on the FFI signatures.

### Refactors

- **Refactor: Extract FrameworkBackend seam from EsastGenPass**: Client codegen (cl.jac / cl {} → JavaScript) is no longer hard-wired to React. A new pluggable `FrameworkBackend` interface and framework-neutral reactive-intent vocabulary (`StateField`, `RefField`, `StateUpdate`, `Effect`, `AsyncBoundary`) allow per-framework lowering. All React-specific emission (`useState`, `useRef`, `useEffect`, `setCount`, `<JacAwaiting>`, `<JacClientErrorBoundary>`) moves into `ReactBackend`. A `[client] framework` config section (default `"react"`) selects the backend at compile time. Unknown framework names now emit `E5081` through the EsastGenPass diagnostic path instead of surfacing as a bare `ValueError`.
- **Feature: Preact backend (Phase 1)**: `framework = "preact"` now selects `PreactBackend`, which reuses React's hooks lowering but imports `useState`/`useEffect`/`useRef` from `preact/hooks`, compiles a Preact-backed `@jac/runtime`, and emits a `render`/`h` entry script.
- **Refactor: Split `client_runtime_core` from the React shim**: Framework-agnostic `@jac/runtime` symbols (auth, walker/function fetch + auto-cache, localStorage, navigation, error reporting) move into `client_runtime_core.cl.jac`; `client_runtime.cl.jac` becomes a thin React/Preact shim that re-exports the core surface so `@jac/runtime` stays one module. The Vite compiler emits the core sibling alongside the shim.
- **Feature: TanStack Form for React and Solid runtimes**: `useJacForm`/`JacForm` now use `@tanstack/react-form` and `@tanstack/solid-form` (Standard Schema validators) instead of `react-hook-form`/`@hookform/resolvers` and `solid-hook-form`. The hand-rolled `__zodResolver` is removed; Zod schemas validate natively through TanStack Form's `validators` API. Peer dependencies, default client deps, and npm publish maps are updated accordingly.
- **Refactor: Impl/test annexes and variants merged into the unified module tree**: `.impl.jac`/`.test.jac` annex bodies and `.sv.jac`/`.cl.jac`/`.na.jac` variant bodies are now spliced into their head module's own tree by a single pass (each spliced statement keeping its own deployment context and file provenance), instead of hanging off `Module.impl_mod`/`test_mod`/`variant_mod` side-lists that the generic walk, sub-node table, and JIR serializer could not see. Every compiler walk, the JIR cache, and tooling now cover annex and variant content directly; the side-list fields and the recompile-on-cache-hit reattachment hack are removed. Cross-variant `impl` matching (a head `.impl.jac` implementing a `.cl.jac`/`.sv.jac` declaration) falls out of the single same-module decl/impl connect.
- **Fix: Auto-lint signature fixing across separate `.impl.jac` files**: `jac format --fix` repairs an impl's parameter list to match its declaration even when the declaration lives in the base file; the auto-lint pass loads the base module's declarations on demand now that each annex is formatted as its own tool program.
- **Fix: Duplicate diagnostics inside matched `impl` bodies**: A type error in a separated `impl` body (e.g. `def f; impl f { ... }`) was reported twice. It is now reported once.
- **Fix: Annex semantic tokens in the language server**: Hovering, go-to-definition, and semantic highlighting inside an `.impl.jac`/`.test.jac` file now resolve again, served per source file by provenance from the merged tree.
- **Refactor: Edge-traversal resolution folds hop-by-hop with no global fallback**: `refs()` walks `ObjectSpatialPath` chains through a new `jaclang.runtimelib.resolver` whose `resolve_path_anchors` calls a uniform per-hop `resolve_hop` at every position. Each hop locally picks index narrowing (when the hop has no predicate filters, has a root anchor, and the input IDs are all owned by that root) or a single-hop `edges_to_nodes` walk fallback (for predicates, foreign-root IDs, missing index, transient origins). The all-or-nothing strategy decision and slow-loop fallback in `planner.execute_path` are gone: `resolve_path_anchors` always returns a `list[NodeAnchor]`, and `refs()` no longer carries a global slow-loop tail. Resolves the fast/slow split described in issue #6778. `planner.execute_path` becomes a one-line wrapper around `resolve_path_anchors` to preserve direct test imports in `test_topology_e2e.jac`. Edge-only queries walk their prefix through the same per-hop fold and then run the existing edge terminator.
- **Refactor: jac-client and jac-desktop now ship with jaclang core**: The client, full-stack, mobile, and desktop project kinds are built into jaclang and no longer require installing the separate `jac-client` / `jac-desktop` packages.
- **Refactor: enhanced console and shadcn/ui now ship with jaclang core**: The Rich-style console output (colors, box-drawn panels and tables, animated spinners) is reimplemented in pure Jac and is now the default, so jaclang stays free of the `rich` dependency. The shadcn/ui system (`jac add --shadcn`, `jac create --use jac-shadcn`, `jac retheme`) is now a built-in provider. The separate `jac-super` package is removed; nothing needs to be installed for either feature.
- **Refactor: Centralize file-extension/module-resolution knowledge**: Suffix lists, the extension-to-codespace mapping, annex detection, and the longest-suffix matching rule (`.cl.jac` outranks `.jac`) now live in one bootstrap-readable registry (`jaclang/jac0core/ext_registry.py`) instead of being re-derived in ~30 places, removing copy-pasted suffix tuples and hand-rolled `endswith` precedence chains. Pure consolidation, no behavior change.
- **Single-binary cleanup**: `jac install <pkg>` and `jac install -e <path>` install into the binary's activated environment (the global/tool-install path that works outside a project); per-project deps go through `jac add` / the no-arg `jac install`, which target the project's `.jac/venv`. The binary discovers a project's `.jac/venv` at startup and gives it `sys.path` precedence, so per-project deps and editable plugins shadow the bundled site. Removes leftover editable-install/packaging scaffolding (`setup.py`, `jaclang.pth`, `MANIFEST.in`) now that jaclang ships only as the native `jac` binary; `sitecustomize.py` is kept but rewritten jaclang-free to wire the project venv and the lazy `.jac` import finder.
- **Build: pure-Zig payload tool (no bash/curl/git/zstd/tar)**: the single-binary payload build's shell scripts (`fetch-pbs.sh`, `fetch-typeshed.sh`, `mkpayload.sh`, `update-typeshed.sh`) are replaced by one std-only Zig tool (`launcher/payload.zig`) that does the HTTP download, checksum verify, (de)compression and tar in Zig's `std`, shelling out only to the bundled CPython for `pip` and the JIR precompile. Build-time host dependencies drop to just `zig` plus a network connection (and an optional, best-effort `strip`). The payload's inner compression switches zstd to gzip so both ends are pure std, the typeshed stubs are fetched over HTTP and verified against a pinned `TARBALL_SHA256`, and the bundled libpython is now stripped, so the shipped binary is slightly smaller than before despite gzip's lower ratio.
- **Refactor: Visitor double-dispatch for compiler passes (native-lowerable)**: The reflective `enter_node`/`exit_node` dispatch in `UniPass`, which selected each pass ability by formatting the runtime class name into `hasattr`/`getattr(self, f"enter_{snake(type(nd).__name__)}")`, is replaced with classic visitor double-dispatch. `enter_node`/`exit_node` now call `nd.accept_enter(self)`/`nd.accept_exit(self)`; each handled node kind has a generated `accept_<verb>` override that calls the pass's `enter_<kind>`/`exit_<kind>` ability directly (a direct, exact-type, O(1) double-vtable call), and unhandled kinds fall through `UniNode`'s base accept to the pass's overridable `default_<verb>` hook. `UniPass` carries a generated `enter_<kind>`/`exit_<kind>` base surface that routes to `default_<verb>`, so a pass ability simply overrides its slot. Run `jac gen-uni-dispatch [--verify]` to (re)generate the `unitree.impl/dispatch.impl.jac` and `uni_pass.impl/surface.impl.jac` annexes. This removes the string-keyed reflection the native backend could not lower (a self-hosting keystone), behaves identically to the old dispatch across every pass and node kind, and drops the per-node name formatting from the CPython build's hot path.

### Documentation

- **Skiils: `jac-cl-routing` skill updated**: Enhance file based routing skills with clarify protected route group behavior.
- **Docs: guides cover desktop IPC, client framework, access enforcement, and third-party stubs**: The `jac guide` skills and the mkdocs reference now document the `@jac/desktop` OS-capability plugins, the `[plugins.client] framework` and `[check] enforce_access` config keys, and installing third-party type stubs via `jac add types-*`.

## jaclang 0.16.7

### Breaking Changes

- **Lambda parameters now require a known type (#6804)**: A lambda whose parameter type cannot be inferred from context, such as a bare `f = lambda x: -x;`, is now a type error (`E1119`) instead of silently typing the parameter as unknown. Annotate the parameter (`lambda x: int : x + 1`; the return type is still inferred) or use the lambda where its type is fixed, e.g. as a typed callback (`sorted(xs, key=lambda x: ...)`) or bound to a `Callable`-typed target.

## jaclang 0.16.6

### New Features

- **Optimistic concurrency for concurrent check-then-create (#6266)**: A walker or function endpoint that does "look it up, create it if missing" against the same node no longer yields duplicate children under concurrency. Each node carries a version; an edge-list write to a node the request *read* is applied with a compare-and-swap, and the request boundary aborts and replays the loser so find-or-create converges on the winner. A blind append (no preceding read) still merges lock-free. The read is recorded independently of how the traversal resolves -- the topology-index/backend fast path and edge-reference reads (`[edge -->]`) take the dependency just as the linear edge-walk does -- and the read snapshot advances after each commit, so a request that commits more than once never conflicts with itself. A new `on_commit(...)` ambient builtin defers external side effects to run exactly once after a successful commit (and is discarded on abort/replay). The policy is configurable in `jac.toml` under `[serve]`: `on_conflict` (`retry`/`fail`), `conflict_max_attempts`, and `conflict_backoff_ms`. The losing unit of work is atomic: `SqliteMemory.apply()` rolls the whole transaction back on a conflict, so a lost race leaves the store unchanged with no orphaned child, and diagnostics accrued by an aborted attempt are cleared so a converged replay's `200` response carries no stale permission warnings. `jac db fsck` now also sweeps *half-linked* edges (cited by only one of their two endpoints) and the nodes they strand, reclaiming any residual orphan. See [Persistence -> Concurrent writes](../../reference/persistence.md#concurrent-writes-check-then-create-and-convergence).
- **New `client` project kind**: Added a `client` project kind for browser-only apps with no backend. `jac run` serves it as a static page (no API server), and `jac build`/`jac start` (via jac-client) produce a portable, self-contained dist.

### Bug Fixes

- **Fix: `glob` declared in an impl annex now resolves on the native (`.na.jac`) backend (#6754)**: A global variable declared in an impl-annex file (`*.na.impl.jac`), rather than the head `.na.jac` file, is now registered in the native module's globals and resolved by references in annexed ability bodies, matching the `@sv` and ecmascript backends. Previously such a reference failed to lower with `error[E5090]: Native pathway does not yet support expression 'Name'` (or `'BinaryExpr'`), an opaque diagnostic that blamed the reference expression rather than the unresolved global, and produced a silently-degraded build when the global only fed a loop bound. The root cause was annex weaving being re-derived per backend at codegen time: `@sv`/ecmascript wove the annex bodies in (`_merge_module_bodies`), while native's statement scan (`iter_context_stmts`) walked only the head module's body. Annex handling is now centralized in the front end: a single `ModuleCodegenPass.iter_woven_segments` is the one source of truth for which statements an annexed module contributes (all three backends derive their woven view from it), a native (`.na.jac`) head's impl/test annexes are coerced to NATIVE code-context once attached -- keyed off the head, so both the canonical bare `foo.impl.jac` and the variant-specific `foo.na.impl.jac` forms are covered -- and type inference runs over annex modules so native codegen finds the types it needs (covering both the same-module and the imported-module cases).
- **Fix: `skip` in an impl-annex walker event ability no longer breaks native `jac test` (#6794)**: A walker event ability that uses `skip` and is split decl/impl -- the `can flood with Area entry;` declaration in the head `.na.jac` and its body in an `impl Walker.flood with Area entry {...}` annex -- compiled and ran correctly on its own, but a native test (or any module) importing it failed with `RuntimeError: native engine unavailable` for every test. The native capability authority accepts `skip` inside a walker `with X entry` event ability (where it lowers as a no-value return) and rejects it in a value-returning function; it found the enclosing ability by walking up to an `Ability` node. When the body lives in an annex the `skip` is enclosed by an `ImplDef` (carrying the `EventSignature` in its `spec`), not an inline `Ability`, so once `iter_context_stmts` began scanning annex bodies (#6754) the authority reached the annex `skip`, saw no enclosing `Ability`, and falsely flagged it as unsupported. That dropped the imported module's LLVM IR (E5090), so linking the importer failed (E5024) and no JIT engine was produced. The capability check now recognizes the decl/impl-split form: a `skip` whose nearest enclosing `ImplDef` has an `EventSignature` is accepted exactly like an inline event-ability `skip`, while a `skip` in a value-returning function (inline or annex) is still rejected.
- **Fix: `sv import` of a node/obj type no longer crashes the client bundle (#6795)**: A `.cl.jac` file that `sv import`s a function together with the node/obj type it returns used to emit two declarations with the same name in the compiled JS, an `async function <Type>()` RPC stub and the wire `class <Type>`, which crashed the bundler with `The symbol "<Type>" has already been declared` even though `jac check` passed. The ecmascript codegen (`EsastGenPass._generate_sv_import_stubs`) was generating an HTTP RPC stub for every imported item regardless of kind; it now skips any item whose resolved symbol is a type (node/obj/edge/enum) or a walker, since a node/obj/edge already lowers to a wire `class`, an enum to a frozen object, and a walker is reached through `__jacSpawn`. Only `def:pub` abilities get an RPC stub. This mirrors the server-side (`sv -> sv`) Python-path fix from #6710.

## jaclang 0.16.5

### New Features

- **Feature: `jac eject` compiles a project into a runnable FastAPI + JavaScript app**: `jac eject` now writes a project-internal `ejected/` folder split into a FastAPI `backend/` (each `.sv.jac`/`.jac` walker compiled to Python and exposed as `POST /walker/<Name>`, functions as `POST /function/<name>`) and a `frontend/` (the `.cl.jac` UI compiled to JavaScript with a Vite setup). The backend runs the walkers on the installed `jaclang` runtime and uses jaclang-native auth: `/user/register` + `/user/login` via `UserManager`, with `:pub` walkers open and the rest token-gated (each user gets their own persistent root graph). One `uvicorn main:app` serves the API and the built frontend. Re-running regenerates the folder without `--force` (it carries a `.jac-ejected` marker), and the output directory is overridable via `[eject].output` in jac.toml.
- **`jac install` now uses `uv` as its pip backend when available**: Dependency installs run through `uv pip` for significantly faster resolution and downloads. A new `--no-uv` flag on `jac install` (or `JAC_NO_UV=1` env var for all install paths) opts back to plain pip.
- **`jac install <pkg>` installs packages into the activated environment (#6703)**: `jac install` now accepts package arguments (e.g. `jac install numpy pandas`), routing them directly to pip against the currently activated Python environment - no `jac.toml` modification. Existing no-arg behavior (`jac install` from a project directory) is unchanged.
- **Feature: User-defined iterators in native code (#6403)**: Any `obj` that implements `__iter__`/`__next__` can now be iterated in the native (`na {}` → LLVM) backend. It works in `for` loops, via first-class `iter()`/`next()`, through the `map()` adapter, and across function boundaries as `Iterator[T]`, with `StopIteration` ending iteration as in Python.

### Bug Fixes

- **Fix: Native and clib type annotations now reject unresolved type names instead of silently defaulting to i64** (issue #6676): C-library import declarations and native-context annotations (`.na.jac` / `na {}`) whose parameter, return, or field type names the compiler cannot resolve are now a hard `E2018` error at `jac check` (not just a `W2001` warning) and are reported honestly at `nacompile` via `E2018`/`E5090`, instead of being silently widened to a signed `i64` at the FFI boundary with a wrong ABI and no diagnostic. A clib declaration with no return arrow (`def f(x: T);`) now correctly lowers its return to `void` (matching an explicit `-> None`) instead of silently declaring the void C function as returning a signed `i64`.
- **Fix: Unresolved object-field type names are now named in the diagnostic, not rendered as `<Unknown>`**: an object field whose annotation names an unresolved type (a typedef'd C handle, an unmodeled width like `uint32_t`) reaches native codegen through a non-expression node, so the `E2018` used to read the useless `Undefined name '<Unknown>'` -- `str()` of the checker's `UnknownType` -- losing the name the user wrote. The label now recovers it from the field's type tag, so the error points at the actual type name. (The front-end `E2018` covers clib/native *signature* positions but not object field declarations, so the codegen pass is currently the sole catcher for bad field types.)
- **Fix: Clear diagnostic for a re-wrapped expression in a JSX slot**: Re-wrapping a single expression in extra `{...}` inside a JSX slot body (`{"text"}`, `{n + 1}`, `{<li/>}`) used to fall through to a misleading `E0002 Missing ';'` that pointed at the *following* line, while the control-flow form (`{if ...}`) got a clear error at the `{`. The redundant expression wrap is now reported as a dedicated error (`E2028`) pointing at the `{` itself: the expression sibling of the control-flow `E2023`, co-located in the parser so the whole redundant-slot-wrap rule lives in one place. The parser recovers by dropping the redundant braces (exactly as the control-flow form does), so the rest of the file still parses without an error cascade. Genuine collection literals (`{1, 2}`, `{a: 1}`) carry a `,`/`:` and are left untouched (#6733).
- **Fix: Bare expression statements in JSX slots no longer silently render nothing**: Inside a JSX `{...}` statement slot, a bare expression statement (a string, f-string, identifier, or call) was evaluated and discarded instead of being added to the slot's children, so conditional content written that way compiled but rendered nothing. Every value-producing expression statement directly inside a slot body is now accumulated as a child, consistent with the `{expr}` slot and bare JSX elements. The misleading `W0060` "docstring" warning that previously fired on such strings is suppressed inside slot bodies (it still fires for genuine misplaced docstrings elsewhere).
- **Fix: `by postinit` fields no longer show a false warning**: A field declared with `has x: T by postinit` was reporting a spurious `W1051` ("Expression type could not be resolved") warning even though the code was correct. The warning is no longer raised.
- **Fix: `jac run`/`jac start` on a `.sv.jac` or `.cl.jac` entry**: Running or serving a server (`.sv.jac`) or client (`.cl.jac`) file directly by path failed with `Cannot find module main.sv` / `No module named 'main.sv'`, because `proc_file` stripped only the trailing `.jac` from the compound codespace suffix and left `main.sv`. It now strips the full suffix for all three compound codespaces (`.na.jac`/`.sv.jac`/`.cl.jac`) so the entry resolves to its bare module stem.
- **Fix: Native `bytes` concatenation and the `bytes()`/`bytearray()` constructors**: `bytes + bytes` no longer crashes native code generation, and `bytes([...])`/`bytearray([...])` now return a length-aware value that preserves embedded NUL bytes, matching the interpreter.
- **Fix: complete the native `bytes` length-aware migration** (issue #6749): the native (`.na.jac` to LLVM) backend made `bytes` a distinct length-aware struct in #6727/#6745, but seven operations still assumed the old NUL-terminated `i8*` representation and either crashed, failed to compile, or returned silently wrong results. They are now all length-aware on the struct, matching the sv (CPython) backend including embedded NUL bytes: repeat (`b * n`), membership (`x in b`, via `memmem` so it sees past NULs), iteration (`for x in b` and `iter(b)`, yielding `int` byte values), truthiness (`if b` and `bool(b)` are emptiness, not a null-pointer test, so empty `bytes` is correctly falsy), `str(b)` (the exact CPython `b'...'` repr with `\t`/`\n`/`\r`/`\\`/`\xNN` escapes and CPython quote selection), `bytes` dict keys (`{b: v}` and `d[b]` compare by value/length instead of pointer identity, so distinct literals and keys differing only by an embedded NUL or length resolve correctly), and ordering (`<`/`>`/`<=`/`>=`, lexicographic over unsigned bytes with a length tiebreak).
- **Fix: null-safe `bytes` comparison against `None` on the native backend** (issue #6751): comparing a `bytes | None` value to `bytes` when the value is `None` no longer crashes or silently drops the result on the native (`.na.jac` to LLVM) backend. The length-aware `bytes` comparison helpers dereferenced both operands unconditionally, so a `None` (a null `bytes` pointer) caused a segfault for a branchy union and silent empty output for a constant `None` (the null load was undefined behavior the optimizer deleted). `==`/`!=` now follow CPython identity semantics (equal only when both operands are `None`, so `None == b"x"` is `False` and `None == None` is `True`) and only read the bytes contents when both operands are non-null, while ordering (`<`/`>`/`<=`/`>=`) against `None` raises `TypeError` to match CPython instead of dereferencing null.
- **Type Checker: Infer unannotated lambda parameter types from the expected callable**: A lambda passed to a generic builtin like `sorted(rows, key=lambda d: d["n"])` no longer reports a false `error[E1054]` ("No matching overload"). The lambda parameter's type is now solved from the call context (the same way `def`-typed callbacks already worked), so the body type-checks, hover shows the inferred type, and the result type is correct. Works for `sorted`, `max`, `min`, `filter`, `zip`, and `enumerate`.

### Documentation

- **Docs: Client skill-guide fixes**: Corrected contradictions and non-compiling examples in the client (cl) skill guides that led AI code generation to emit broken Jac (file-based-vs-manual routing rule, subscript hook/server-result access, and verified sorting + number-formatting recipes).

## jaclang 0.16.4

### New Features

- **Feature: Kind-aware `jac create`**: `jac create --kind <kind>` scaffolds a project for a specific project kind, stamping `[project] kind` into `jac.toml` and laying the entry-point in the right codespace so the new project's bare `jac run` dispatches deterministically (execute / serve / build). The eight core kinds (cli, native-app, native-binary, shared-library, api-service, microservices, pypi-package, npm-package) ship with `jaclang`; plugin kinds fail fast with an install hint. `--kind` and `--use` are mutually exclusive, and `jac create --list_jacpacks` now lists the available kinds and named variants. The `register_project_template` hook is now aggregating (was first-result), so every installed plugin contributes its kind templates.
- **Feature: `isinstance` on an `any` value in native code**: The native (`na {}` → LLVM) backend now lowers `isinstance(x, T)` for `int`, `bool`, `float`, `str`, `list`, `dict`, `set`, and tuples of those (`isinstance(x, (int, str))`). It works whether `x` is an `any`/`JacVal` (runtime tag check) or a concrete value (folds to a constant), reusing the existing `JacVal` box scheme. `bool` is now boxed under its own tag so it stays distinguishable from `int`, matching CPython's `bool ⊂ int` (`isinstance(True, bool)` and `isinstance(True, int)` are both true, `isinstance(5, bool)` is false). Assigning an explicit `any` into a concrete-typed slot (`z: int = a`) is also allowed in native context now, unboxing at the coercion seam to stay congruent with the sv pathway. This unblocks generic-over-`any` Mechanism-B stdlib code (`json`, `collections`, …) in the native standard-library roadmap (#6404).
